</p>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://lecrae.com">lecrae<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Lecrae Devaughn Moore</b> (born October 9, 1979) is an American <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapper</a>, singer, songwriter, <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record</a> and <a href="/wiki/Film_producer" title="Film producer">film producer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Record_executive" class="mw-redirect" title="Record executive">record executive</a>, actor, and entrepreneur.
</p><p>He is the president, co-owner and co-founder of the independent record label <a href="/wiki/Reach_Records" title="Reach Records">Reach Records</a>, was the co-founder and president of the now-defunct non-profit organization ReachLife Ministries, is an investor and co-owner of the audio production software MXD, and is a co-founder of the film production studio 3 Strand Films. To date, he has released ten studio albums and three mixtapes as a solo artist, and has released three studio albums, a remix album, one EP, and numerous singles as the leader of the hip hop group <a href="/wiki/116_Clique" class="mw-redirect" title="116 Clique">116 Clique</a>. He produced much of his earlier material along with other early Reach Records releases. Lecrae, in reference to him being labeled as a Christian rapper, has stated that his music is just hip hop, though it reflects his Christian faith. In May 2016, Lecrae signed to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> in a joint deal between his label and Columbia. He left Columbia in May 2020.
</p><p>Lecrae's debut recording, <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Talk_(Lecrae_album)" title="Real Talk (Lecrae album)">Real Talk</a></i>, was released in 2004 through Reach Records. His third solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rebel_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rebel (Lecrae album)">Rebel</a></i>, released in 2008, became the first Christian hip-hop album to reach No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> Gospel chart. <i><a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rehab (Lecrae album)">Rehab</a></i> followed in 2010, and Lecrae began attracting mainstream attention when he performed at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> Hip Hop Awards Cypher and appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Statik_Selektah" title="Statik Selektah">Statik Selektah</a> song "Live &amp; Let Live" from <i><a href="/wiki/Population_Control_(album)" title="Population Control (album)">Population Control</a></i>. On May 10, 2012, Lecrae released his first mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Church_Clothes" title="Church Clothes">Church Clothes</a></i>, which was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Don_Cannon" title="Don Cannon">Don Cannon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-illhype_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illhype-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Considered his breakthrough into mainstream hip hop, the mixtape was downloaded over 100,000 times in less than 48 hours. His sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(Lecrae_album)" title="Gravity (Lecrae album)">Gravity</a></i>, came out on September 4, 2012, and has been called the most important album in Christian hip hop history by <a href="/wiki/Rapzilla" title="Rapzilla">Rapzilla</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Daily_World" title="Atlanta Daily World">Atlanta Daily World</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-rapzillareview2_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapzillareview2-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted as the best-selling album overall in the iTunes Store,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> No. 3 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Gospel_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Gospel Album">Grammy Award for Best Gospel Album</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Grammy Awards">2013 Grammy Awards</a>, marking the first time that a hip hop artist received this award. Lecrae released his seventh album, <i><a href="/wiki/Anomaly_(Lecrae_album)" title="Anomaly (Lecrae album)">Anomaly</a></i>, on September 9, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with 88,587 copies sold through the first week,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> the first album to top both the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and the Gospel chart simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He released a third mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Church_Clothes_3" title="Church Clothes 3">Church Clothes 3</a></i>, on January 15, 2016, an eighth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Work_Together" title="All Things Work Together">All Things Work Together</a></i>, on September 22, 2017, and a ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Let_the_Trap_Say_Amen" title="Let the Trap Say Amen">Let the Trap Say Amen</a></i>, a collaborative project with <a href="/wiki/Zaytoven" title="Zaytoven">Zaytoven</a>, on June 22, 2018. His tenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Restoration_(Lecrae_album)" title="Restoration (Lecrae album)">Restoration</a></i>, was released on August 21, 2020.
</p><p>Lecrae received nominations for Artist of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/43rd_GMA_Dove_Awards" title="43rd GMA Dove Awards">43rd</a>, <a href="/wiki/44th_GMA_Dove_Awards" title="44th GMA Dove Awards">44th</a>, 45th, and <a href="/wiki/46th_GMA_Dove_Awards" title="46th GMA Dove Awards">46th</a> <a href="/wiki/GMA_Dove_Award" title="GMA Dove Award">GMA Dove Awards</a>, the last of which he won, and for <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Best_Gospel_Artist" class="mw-redirect" title="BET Award for Best Gospel Artist">Best Gospel Artist</a> at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2013" title="BET Awards 2013">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2015" title="BET Awards 2015">2015 BET Awards</a>, the latter of which he won, a first for a rap artist. Lecrae's filmography includes a role in the television film <i>A Cross to Bear</i> (2012) and brief roles in the comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Believe_Me_(film)" title="Believe Me (film)">Believe Me</a></i> (2014), crime film <i><a href="/wiki/Superfly_(2018_film)" title="Superfly (2018 film)">Superfly</a></i> (2018), and Christian drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_(2019_film)" title="Breakthrough (2019 film)">Breakthrough</a></i> (2019). In the social sphere, Lecrae has presented on and written about <a href="/wiki/Race_relations_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Race relations in the United States">racial tension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_States" title="Racism in the United States">injustice</a> in the United States as well as advocated for the preservation of responsibility and fatherhood values among men in the United States. In 2013 he partnered with <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_DuBois" title="Joshua DuBois">Joshua DuBois</a> in the multimedia initiative <i>This Is Fatherhood</i> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama" title="Presidency of Barack Obama">Obama administration</a>'s Fatherhood and Mentoring Initiative, and in 2020 during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> worked with Love Beyond Walls to distribute hand-washing stations and food to homeless people in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lecrae was raised by his single mother in a poor neighborhood in southern <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Blackburn_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blackburn-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after his birth, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, away from his father, then to <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> At the age of 6, he was sexually abused by his babysitter.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> As a teenager, his role models were the rapper <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> and his uncle, a member of a street gang. <sup id="cite_ref-Landrum_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landrum-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age 16, he began using <a href="/wiki/Drugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Drugs">drugs</a>, trying almost every substance except crack and <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wete_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wete-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He started stealing in high school and dealing drugs, using his grandmother's <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> as a lucky charm.<sup id="cite_ref-Almasy_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Almasy-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He was arrested for possession of drugs, but the policeman who arrested him discovered his Bible and made him promise that, if he let Lecrae go, he would live according to biblical principles from now on. Subsequently, he began <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">rehab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Landrum_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landrum-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He dropped drugs but replaced them with alcohol and partying.
</p><p>Lecrae received a scholarship to study theater at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Texas" title="University of North Texas">University of North Texas</a>, and graduated with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Applied_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Bachelor of Applied Arts and Sciences">Bachelor of Applied Arts and Sciences</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Blackburn_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blackburn-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He also briefly attended <a href="/wiki/Middle_Tennessee_State_University" title="Middle Tennessee State University">Middle Tennessee State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 19, he went to a <a href="/wiki/Bible_study_(Christianity)" title="Bible study (Christianity)">Bible study</a> after being invited by a girl from college.<sup id="cite_ref-Wete_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wete-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He was amazed to see people like himself there, who liked the same books and music, but who were loving. He decided to live for God, but continued to make bad choices. Following a friend's invitation, he attended a Christian conference in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> and was impressed by the performance of a Christian rap group, <a href="/wiki/The_Cross_Movement" title="The Cross Movement">The Cross Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He was also touched by a clear presentation of the gospel by Pastor James White (of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cokcc.org/leadership">Christ Our King Community Church</a>). He then asked forgiveness for his sins and claimed to have experienced a <a href="/wiki/New_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="New birth">new birth</a>.
</p><p>Subsequently, he was in a car accident but came out unscathed.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blackburn_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blackburn-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, in a Bible study meeting at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dentonbible.org/">Denton Bible Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denton,_Texas" title="Denton, Texas">Denton, Texas</a>, he met Ben Washer, with whom he would volunteer and sing in a <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_correctional_facility" class="mw-redirect" title="Juvenile correctional facility">juvenile correctional facility</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>Young people's positive response to Christian rap encouraged them to start a label.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Early_career_.282004.E2.80.932011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_(2004–2011)">Early career (2004–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career (2004–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, five years after his conversion, Lecrae teamed up with Ben Washer to found <a href="/wiki/Reach_Records" title="Reach Records">Reach Records</a>, and at the age of 25 he released his first album, <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Talk_(Lecrae_album)" title="Real Talk (Lecrae album)">Real Talk</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The following year it was re-released by <a href="/wiki/Cross_Movement_Records" title="Cross Movement Records">Cross Movement Records</a> and reached No. 29 on the <i>Billboard</i> Gospel Albums chart, staying on the chart for 12 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The album later received a nomination at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Stellar_Awards" title="Stellar Awards">Stellar Awards</a>. In 2005, Lecrae co-founded the non-profit organization ReachLife Ministries (no longer operational since April 2015),<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> which equipped local Christian leaders with tools, media, curriculum, and conferences that were based on the teachings of the Bible and relevant to hip-hop culture.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2005, the debut album of 116 Clique, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Compilation_Album" class="mw-redirect" title="The Compilation Album">The Compilation Album</a></i>, was released.<sup id="cite_ref-116clique_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116clique-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the success of <i>Real Talk</i>, Lecrae then released his second studio album on August 15, 2006. <i>After the Music Stops</i> charted at No. 5 on the <i>Billboard</i> Gospel Albums chart, No. 7 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Top_Christian_Albums" title="Top Christian Albums">Christian Albums</a> chart and No. 16 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Heatseekers" class="mw-redirect" title="Heatseekers">Heatseeker Album</a> charts,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and received a nomination for a <a href="/wiki/Dove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Dove Award">Dove Award</a>, as did the single "<a href="/wiki/Jesus_Muzik" title="Jesus Muzik">Jesus Muzik</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Trip_Lee" title="Trip Lee">Trip Lee</a>. In 2007, 116 Clique released its second album, <i><a href="/wiki/13_Letters" title="13 Letters">13 Letters</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-116clique_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116clique-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> reaching No. 10 on the Gospel Albums chart and No. 29 on the Christian Albums chart.<sup id="cite_ref-116charts_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116charts-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> 116 Clique also released the <a href="/wiki/Remix_album" title="Remix album">remix EP</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Amped_(116_Clique_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amped (116 Clique album)">Amped</a></i>, which peaked at No. 24 on the Gospel Albums chart.<sup id="cite_ref-116charts_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116charts-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 8, 2008, Lecrae's third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rebel_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rebel (Lecrae album)">Rebel</a></i>, entered the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> charts at No. 60 with 9,800 units sold and topped the <i>Billboard</i> Gospel Album charts for two weeks, the first hip-hop album to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It also charted at No. 2 on the Christian Albums chart and No. 15 on the Top Independent charts.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the album received a nomination at the 40th Dove Awards, as did the <a href="/wiki/Flame_(rapper)" title="Flame (rapper)">Flame</a> song "Joyful Noise", which featured Lecrae and John Reilly.<sup id="cite_ref-40thdoove_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40thdoove-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> 2009 also saw Lecrae's first film role, when he appeared in the documentary <i>Uprise Presents: Word from the Street</i> by the UK-based TV channel OHTV.<sup id="cite_ref-uprise_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprise-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> and he helped establish Blueprint Church (<a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>). <sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 5, 2010, Lecrae released a <a href="/wiki/Charity_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Charity single">charity single</a> entitled "Far Away", a tribute to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>. Lecrae promised that all proceeds from the single's sales would go directly to the Haiti relief effort.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On July 7, Lecrae announced on the Reach Records website that the title of his new album would be <i><a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rehab (Lecrae album)">Rehab</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On August 5, 2010, Rapzilla shared a new song from Lecrae called "Amp It Up".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae subsequently clarified on his Twitter account that the song was not a single from <i>Rehab</i>, but rather a theme song for Kanakuk Kamps, a chain of Christian camps for which he writes songs annually.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On August 31, 2010, Reach Records revealed the track list for <i>Rehab</i>, released it for pre-order, and premiered a promotional video "Idols".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A second promotional video, entitled "I Am Dust", debuted on September 9, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Upon its release, <i>Rehab</i> hit No. 16 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart, making it one of the highest selling Christian hip hop albums at that time.
</p><p>On September 22, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Rapzilla" title="Rapzilla">Rapzilla</a> reported that the <i>Rehab</i> packaging came with an advertisement encouraging buyers to purchase another upcoming album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rehab:_The_Overdose" title="Rehab: The Overdose">Rehab: The Overdose</a></i>, which saw release on January 11, 2011. It included 11 new songs and featured several other Christian artists such as Thi'sl and <a href="/wiki/Swoope_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Swoope (rapper)">Swoope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i>Rehab: The Overdose</i> debuted at No. 15 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200. On August 29, 2011, Lecrae announced through Twitter that on September 27, 2011, he would release a special edition of <i>Rehab</i>, entitled <i>Rehab: Deluxe Edition</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, 116 Clique released their fourth album, entitled <i>Man Up</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On September 7, 2011, Rapzilla announced that Lecrae would be featured on the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a> Cypher on October 11, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae gained popularity after his verse on the cypher trended nationwide on Twitter and was featured on <a href="/wiki/AllHipHop" title="AllHipHop">AllHipHop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-God_Son_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-God_Son-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae then appeared as a feature on <a href="/wiki/Statik_Selektah" title="Statik Selektah">Statik Selektah</a>'s song "Live and Let Live" from his <i><a href="/wiki/Population_Control_(album)" title="Population Control (album)">Population Control</a></i> album.
</p>
<h3><span id="Mainstream_breakthrough_.282012.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainstream_breakthrough_(2012–2016)">Mainstream breakthrough (2012–2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mainstream breakthrough (2012–2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg/220px-Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg/330px-Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg/440px-Billboard12-crayola-lecrae.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Lecrae (left) and <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a> (right) at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2013 Billboard Music Awards">2013 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On February 16, 2012, Rapzilla announced that Lecrae was preparing to release his first mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Church_Clothes" title="Church Clothes">Church Clothes</a></i>. On May 3, 2012, Lecrae premiered his music video for the title track of his <i>Church Clothes</i> mixtape online on <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-christianpostvideo_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christianpostvideo-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The video was noted for including cameos by <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a>, and attracted almost 20,000 views in less than a day.<sup id="cite_ref-christianpostvideo_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christianpostvideo-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Hosted by <a href="/wiki/Don_Cannon" title="Don Cannon">Don Cannon</a>, the mixtape featured the song <i>Darkest Hour</i>, in which Lecrae collaborated with No Malice of <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <i>Church Clothes</i> was downloaded more than 100,000 times in less than 48 hours on DatPiff.com, and in less than a month reached 250,000 downloads, a platinum rating on the website.<sup id="cite_ref-jamz_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jamz-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On June 25, 2012, a <a href="/wiki/Remastered" class="mw-redirect" title="Remastered">remastered</a> version of the mixtape, without DJ Don Cannon, was released as an <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> for sale on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-epversion_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epversion-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Due to issues with <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">sampling</a>, this version was much shorter with only seven songs.<sup id="cite_ref-epversion_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epversion-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Upon its release, the EP debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts"><i>Billboard</i> charts</a> at No. 10 on both the Christian Albums and Gospel Albums charts for the week of July 14, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ituneschart_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ituneschart-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-christianalbums_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christianalbums-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gospelalbums_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gospelalbums-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 27, Lecrae announced that his next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(Lecrae_album)" title="Gravity (Lecrae album)">Gravity</a></i>, was to be released in late 2012, and recording sessions began in May.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On June 21, 2012, Lecrae appeared live at the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">Apple Store</a> in Chicago for Black Music Month.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The release date for <i>Gravity</i>, September 4, 2012, as well as the album artwork was announced on July 19, 2012, via Rapzilla.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 30, 2012, the rapper <a href="/wiki/Saigon_(rapper)" title="Saigon (rapper)">Saigon</a> announced that Lecrae would be one of the featured artists on his upcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Greatest_Story_Never_Told_Chapter_2:_Bread_and_Circuses" title="The Greatest Story Never Told Chapter 2: Bread and Circuses">The Greatest Story Never Told Chapter 2: Bread and Circuses</a></i>, due November 6, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Gravity</i> was released on September 4, 2012, to critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-houston_press_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houston_press-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Upon its release, <i>Gravity</i> debuted at No. 3 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, with 72,000 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard#3_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard#3-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The album also debuted at No. 1 on the Christian, Gospel, Independent, and Rap Album charts, No. 3 on the Digital Albums chart, and 24 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> After the iTunes deluxe version of the album hit No. 1 on that vendors charts, and the regular version at number No. 2, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> wrote an article about Lecrae and his success with the album.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 7, 2013, Lecrae released his second mixtape, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Church_Clothes_Vol._2" class="mw-redirect" title="Church Clothes Vol. 2">Church Clothes Vol. 2</a></i>, hosted once again by Don Cannon. The mixtape debuted at No.&#160;21 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, No.&#160;1 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> Christian Albums and Gospel Albums charts, and No.&#160;3 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_Rap_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Rap Albums">Rap Albums</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-albums_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albums-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On Datpiff.com, the album was download over 146,000 times by November 26, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-datpiff_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-datpiff-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 3, 2014, Lecrae announced through social media that his seventh studio album would be titled <i><a href="/wiki/Anomaly_(Lecrae_album)" title="Anomaly (Lecrae album)">Anomaly</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The album released on September 9, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> It is supported by the single "Nuthin".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at No. 1 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">Billboard 200</a></i> with over 88,000 copies sold through the first week. It is the first time an album tops both the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and the Gospel Albums chart. Lecrae also became the fifth artist following <a href="/wiki/Chris_Tomlin" title="Chris Tomlin">Chris Tomlin</a> (2013), <a href="/wiki/TobyMac" title="TobyMac">TobyMac</a> (2012), <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a> (1997) and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Carlisle" title="Bob Carlisle">Bob Carlisle</a> (1997) to score a number one album on both Christian Albums and the <i>Billboard</i> 200. <i>Anomaly</i> also marks the sixth time that Lecrae topped the Gospel Albums chart and the fifth time he topped the Christian Albums chart.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In its second week of sales, the album sold 31,000 copies, bringing the total to 120,000 copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In its third week of sales, the album sold another 17,000 copies, bringing the total to 137,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <i>Anomaly</i> went on to sell over 500,000 copies, and was certified Gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> on August 26, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> As a reward to fans for their support in helping his album go No. 1 on <i>Billboard</i>, Lecrae released a new song, "Non-Fiction", as a free download on September 17.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The song was subsequently released on October 21, 2014, in the iTunes store.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The single "All I Need Is You" from the album was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance">Best Rap Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/57th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="57th Annual Grammy Awards">57th Annual Grammy Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and on June 12, 2019, the song was certified Gold by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To promote <i>Anomaly</i>, on September 18, 2014, Lecrae appeared on <a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a>, performing alongside <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>, the program's <a href="/wiki/House_band" title="House band">house band</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> He made a subsequent appearance the following year, on January 9, 2015, this time as a featured performer.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On January 15, 2016, Lecrae released his third mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Church_Clothes_3" title="Church Clothes 3">Church Clothes 3</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape debuted at No. 12 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and No. 1 on the Christian, Rap, and Independent charts, selling some 29,207 units.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Signing_with_Columbia_and_Restoration_.282016.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Signing_with_Columbia_and_Restoration_(2016–present)">Signing with Columbia and <i>Restoration</i> (2016–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Signing with Columbia and Restoration (2016–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni,_Japan,_Jan._9,_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg/220px-Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="230" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg/330px-Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg/440px-Lecrae_at_Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Iwakuni%2C_Japan%2C_Jan._9%2C_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="465" /></a><figcaption>Lecrae performing a free concert at Marine Corps Air Station, <a href="/wiki/Iwakuni" title="Iwakuni">Iwakuni</a>, Japan, January 9, 2018.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In August 2015, Lecrae announced an upcoming memoir titled <i>Unashamed</i>, which on May 3, 2016, was published through B&amp;H Publishing Group, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/LifeWay_Christian_Resources" title="LifeWay Christian Resources">LifeWay Christian Resources</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It opened at No. 19 on <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_list" title="The New York Times Best Seller list">The New York Times Best Seller list</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In May 2016, Lecrae signed to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a>, which will release future recordings in conjunction with Reach.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae explained that he signed this deal in order to increase the international audience for Reach, since his label peaked nationally with the release of <i>Anomaly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016, Reach Records announced Lecrae's upcoming tour schedule, The Destination Tour (You're Accepted), which ran through October and November.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On October 21, 2016, Lecrae released the single "Can't Stop Me Now (Destination)", the lead single from his upcoming studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On January 27, 2017, he released the second single "Blessings", featuring <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_Sign" title="Ty Dolla Sign">Ty Dolla Sign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae followed this up with the third single "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Find_You" title="I&#39;ll Find You">I'll Find You</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Tori_Kelly" title="Tori Kelly">Tori Kelly</a>, on June 8, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Then, on June 23, 2017, he released a promotional single "Hammer Time", featuring 1K Phew.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On August 7, 2017, Lecrae announced his eighth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Work_Together_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="All Things Work Together (album)">All Things Work Together</a></i>, his major label debut.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on September 22, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> "Blessings" went on to be certified Gold on April 30, 2019, and "I'll Find You" was certified Platinum on February 26, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 24, 2018, he announced in a DJ Booth editorial that he and producer <a href="/wiki/Zaytoven" title="Zaytoven">Zaytoven</a> would release a collaborative album called <i><a href="/wiki/Let_the_Trap_Say_Amen_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Let the Trap Say Amen (album)">Let the Trap Say Amen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on June 22, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In December 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">Atlanta Hawks</a> accidentally leaked information about a new Lecrae album coming March 2020 when they posted about a Lecrae performance—also in March—that included information about the album: <i>Restoration</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with Black Enterprise, Lecrae said that he is excited to put out some healing music, that there is always "hope, healing, and restoration available if you seek it". In the same interview, Lecrae discussed his forthcoming second book, <i>I Am Restored: How I Lost My Religion but Found My Faith</i>, which will be a follow-up to his first book <i>Unashamed</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <i>I Am Restored</i> will release October 13, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The first single to <i>Restoration</i>, "Set Me Free", featuring <a href="/wiki/YK_Osiris" title="YK Osiris">YK Osiris</a>, and the accompanying music video, was released on March 20, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In May 2020, Lecrae left Columbia, and stated that this would give him more artistic freedom and control.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Restoration_(Lecrae_album)" title="Restoration (Lecrae album)">Restoration</a></i> was released on August 21, 2020. On December 3, 2021, Lecrae released <i>No Church In a While</i>, a ten-track collaboration album with 1K Phew.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences_and_musical_style">Influences and musical style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Influences and musical style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lecrae's musical genre is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">Southern hip hop</a> and has been described as falling under the styles of <a href="/wiki/Crunk" title="Crunk">crunk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip_hop" title="Hardcore hip hop">hardcore hip hop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> On his third release, <i><a href="/wiki/Rebel_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rebel (Lecrae album)">Rebel</a></i>, Lecrae slowed down his style on many songs.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Lecrae_album)" title="Rehab (Lecrae album)">Rehab</a></i> was noted for its stylistic diversity, particularly on the song "Children of the Light", which featured Dillavou and <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Sandoval" title="Sonny Sandoval">Sonny Sandoval</a> and incorporated rock, and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> With the release <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(Lecrae_album)" title="Gravity (Lecrae album)">Gravity</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> described Lecrae as incorporating reggae and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> influences into his "signature brash sound."<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <i>Let the Trap Say Amen</i> blended Lecrae's spiritual lyrics with <a href="/wiki/Zaytoven" title="Zaytoven">Zaytoven</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Trap_music" title="Trap music">trap</a>-style production.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Regarding which musical artists have influenced him, Lecrae, in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Essence_(magazine)" title="Essence (magazine)">Essence</a></i>, cited <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Quik" title="DJ Quik">DJ Quik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarface_(rapper)" title="Scarface (rapper)">Scarface</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Cross_Movement" title="The Cross Movement">The Cross Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Post" title="The Christian Post">The Christian Post</a></i>, Lecrae listed his top favorite five hip hop artists as <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Ambassador_(rapper)" title="The Ambassador (rapper)">The Ambassador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>, though he admires Jay-Z for his business approach rather than his music.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae also names <a href="/wiki/Outkast" title="Outkast">Outkast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a> as major influences, particularly their albums <i><a href="/wiki/Aquemini" title="Aquemini">Aquemini</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miseducation_of_Lauryn_Hill" title="The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill">The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill</a></i>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> He considers Hill's song "Adam Lives in Theory" the top song that nourishes him spiritually.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In the song "Non-Fiction", he lists the <a href="/wiki/Tunnel_Rats_(music_group)" title="Tunnel Rats (music group)">Tunnel Rats</a> alongside The Cross Movement as an influence when he was newly converted to Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Theologically, Lecrae follows the <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Reformed tradition</a> and is considered an influential figure in the <a href="/wiki/New_Calvinism" title="New Calvinism">New Calvinist</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> He cites Tommy Nelson, <a href="/wiki/John_F._MacArthur" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. MacArthur">John MacArthur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Piper_(theologian)" title="John Piper (theologian)">John Piper</a>, among others, as early influences on his Christian faith, and Lecrae even titled one of his songs, "Don't Waste Your Life", after the book of the same name by Piper.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae explains that through Nelson, MacArthur, and Piper, he subsequently discovered <a href="/wiki/Charles_Spurgeon" title="Charles Spurgeon">Charles Spurgeon</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Schaeffer" title="Francis Schaeffer">Francis Schaeffer</a>, the last of whom Lecrae calls his "personal hero".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Other theologians cited by Lecrae include <a href="/wiki/Tim_Keller_(pastor)" title="Tim Keller (pastor)">Tim Keller</a>, Andy Crouch, Randy Alcorn, and <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Kuyper" title="Abraham Kuyper">Abraham Kuyper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> He also looks to <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a> for inspiration on working out faith in application to social issues.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_New_Times" title="Miami New Times">Miami New Times</a></i>, he frequently tells the press: "My music is not Christian, Lecrae is."  He continues: "I think Christian is a wonderful noun, but a terrible adjective. Are there Christian shoes, Christian clothes, Christian plumbers, Christian pipes? I think if you're going to, you should label it hip-hop... hip-hop is a particular poetic style. Labeling it with the faith assumes that the song is going to be some kind of sermon, but there's a lot of social and political things that I don't think make it gospel or Christian music." He also stated, "I like to wrap my mind around a total situation. I'm a social anthropologist. If I never been homeless, let me try to be homeless for a week and soak up that information. More like a method actor. So for me it's spending time with people and talking about things from their perspective."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a> guard <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Lin" title="Jeremy Lin">Jeremy Lin</a> recommended Lecrae and <a href="/wiki/Hillsong_United_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsong United (band)">Hillsong</a> in an interview when asked about his pre-game music.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Former NFL quarterback <a href="/wiki/Tim_Tebow" title="Tim Tebow">Tim Tebow</a> and professional wrestler <a href="/wiki/Ezekiel_Jackson" title="Ezekiel Jackson">Ezekiel Jackson</a> have also endorsed Lecrae.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> During March 2014, Lecrae signed a ten-day contract with the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">Atlanta Hawks</a>, and on April 4, 2014, he performed live at <a href="/wiki/Philips_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Philips Arena">Philips Arena</a> after the Hawks game.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> "Dum Dum", a song by <a href="/wiki/Tedashii" title="Tedashii">Tedashii</a> featuring Lecrae, was used on an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/So_You_Think_You_Can_Dance" title="So You Think You Can Dance">So You Think You Can Dance</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae also created the theme song for a new <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> <i><a href="/wiki/SportsCenter" title="SportsCenter">SportsCenter</a></i> block called "Coast to Coast".<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_activism">Social activism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Social activism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm/220px--Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" height="124" data-durationhint="86" data-mwtitle="Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b0/Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm/Lecrae_on_fatherhood_and_sex_trafficking.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; <p>In 2011, 116 Clique and ReachLife Ministries, both headed by Lecrae, launched a media campaign titled <i>Man Up</i>, intended to mentor male urban youths on fatherhood and biblical manhood.<sup id="cite_ref-manup_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manup-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> It features concert tours and a curriculum centered on a short film and a studio album, both titled <i>Man Up</i>, and since 2012 has also featured a string of conference events.<sup id="cite_ref-manup_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manup-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Lecrae partnered with <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> player <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a>, filmmaker Art Hooker, and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_DuBois" title="Joshua DuBois">Joshua DuBois</a>, the former head of the <a href="/wiki/White_House_Office_of_Faith-Based_and_Neighborhood_Partnerships" title="White House Office of Faith-Based and Neighborhood Partnerships">Office of Faith Based and Neighborhood Partnerships</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama" title="Presidency of Barack Obama">Obama administration</a>, to create the national media campaign <i>This Is Fatherhood</i>, an initiative "devoted to restoring America's commitment to healthy fatherhood."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The campaign began on May 1 with a "This is Fatherhood Challenge", in which contestants could submit videos, songs, and essays about fatherhood through June 10. The winners received cash prizes and a trip to Washington, D.C., for a ceremony on <a href="/wiki/Father%27s_Day_(United_States)" title="Father&#39;s Day (United States)">Father's Day</a>. In addition, Lecrae offered studio time and mentoring to the grand prize winner.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Lecrae, Wade, DuBois, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>, and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> all made appearances in the campaign's promotional public service announcements.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lecrae has also contributed op-ed articles to <i>Billboard</i> dealing with <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_States" title="Racism in the United States">race relations in the United States</a>, including the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Ferguson_unrest" title="Ferguson unrest">Ferguson unrest</a>, 2015 <a href="/wiki/Charleston_church_shooting" title="Charleston church shooting">Charleston church shooting</a>, and 2016 shootings of <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Alton_Sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of Alton Sterling">Alton Stirling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Philando_Castile" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of Philando Castile">Philando Castile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_shooting_of_Dallas_police_officers" title="2016 shooting of Dallas police officers">five Dallas police officers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In these articles, Lecrae has called for understanding and empathy across racial divides and willingness to listen to the oppressed, and also pointed out the need for spiritual healing through Jesus Christ.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In mid 2016, Lecrae did a talk about racial reconciliation at <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, titled "Knowledge through Narrative: Bridging the Racial Divide in America".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> He also spoke on hip hop culture at a Nashville TEDx conference, decrying the misogyny and violence rampant in much of hip hop's lyrics but advocating for hip hop to be used as an agent for social change.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2016_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2016 BET Hip Hop Awards">2016 BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, Lecrae performed an original composition addressing racial injustice in the United States, referencing the <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Philando_Castile" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of Philando Castile">shooting of Philando Castile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Lecrae worked with a local non-profit, Love Beyond Walls, to distribute hand-washing stations and food to homeless people in Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> He also wrote an essay for <i>Billboard</i> in which he discussed the need for humane behavior in the midst of widespread social panic due to the outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_George_Floyd" title="Murder of George Floyd">murder of George Floyd</a>, Lecrae was inspired to write "Deep End",<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> which was a late addition to <i>Restoration</i>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_business_ventures">Other business ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other business ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lecrae has partnered with Oust Labs to be an investor and co-owner of the audio production software MXD, which was founded by Jacob "Biz" Morris.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Lecrae teamed up with Adam Thomason to found the film production studio 3 Strand Films.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> He is a venture partner in Collab Capital,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and has participated in several real estate ventures, including Invest Atlanta and Peace Preparatory Academy, intended to revitalize <a href="/wiki/English_Avenue_and_Vine_City" title="English Avenue and Vine City">English Avenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lecrae currently resides in Atlanta since relocating there from Memphis in 2009, and is married to Darragh Moore. The couple have three children together.<sup id="cite_ref-familychristian_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-familychristian-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/HipHopDX" title="HipHopDX">HipHopDX</a>, Lecrae stated that <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a> member <a href="/wiki/No_Malice" title="No Malice">No Malice</a> sought him out as a spiritual advisor.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On October 20, 2016, Lecrae wrote in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i> that he has been struggling with depression and doubt, which was partly caused by the backlash he received from many <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">American evangelicals</a> who are critical of his public stance on race-related issues.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> On August 14, 2020, Lecrae posted a video on his YouTube channel that includes footage of him re-connecting with his long-absent father who now resides in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li><i>I Am Restored: How I Lost My Religion but Found My Faith</i> (October 13, 2020)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lecrae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Lecrae" title="List of awards and nominations received by Lecrae">List of awards and nominations received by Lecrae</a></div>
<p>In 2016, he received an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_doctorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary doctorate">honorary doctorate</a> in music from the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Christian_College" title="Canada Christian College">Canada Christian College</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Whitby_(Ontario)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Whitby (Ontario) (page does not exist)">Whitby (Ontario)</a> for his commitment to sharing a message of hope with disadvantaged young people.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lecrae has won many music awards over the space of his career, including two Grammy Awards and eight <a href="/wiki/Dove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Dove Award">Dove Awards</a>. In 2013, he became the first hip hop artist to win the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Gospel_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Gospel Album">Grammy Award for Best Gospel Album</a>, which was awarded to his sixth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(Lecrae_album)" title="Gravity (Lecrae album)">Gravity</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and in 2015 became the first rapper to win the <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Best_Gospel_Artist" class="mw-redirect" title="BET Award for Best Gospel Artist">BET Award for Best Gospel Artist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
